<b>lapya</b> <i>n</i> lapping or dashing of waves, sound
of waves coming onto the shore. <i>Ang lapya
sa mga balud sa baybáyun,</i> The lapping of
the waves on the shore. <i>v</i> [A; b6] for the
waves to strike the shore. <b>lapyahan, lapyahánan</b>
<i>n</i> the place where the waves strike
the shore. <b>-in-</b> <i>n</i> sound of waves striking the
shore.

<b>lapyà</b> <i>a</i> @broad in face, flattened out. <i>Lapyag
nawung,</i> A broad, @flat face. <i>v</i> [B] be, become
flattened out. <i>Nalapyà ang nígu nga
naligsan sa trák,</i> The winnowing tray is flattened
out because the truck drove over it.

<b>lapyat</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> @fat and @flabby. <i>Dalágang úlay kunu
piru lapyat na ug dughan,</i> She's supposed
to be a virgin but she has sagging breasts. <b>2</b>
slow and languid in movement. <i>Lapyat nga
manlihuklihuk,</i> Moving sluggishly. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B; a2]
be, become flabby or lacking in fullness.
<i>Wà kay iksirsayis maung nagkalapyat ang
ímung buktun,</i> You lack exercise. No wonder
your arms are getting flabby. <b>2</b> [B; a2]
move without energy. <i>Dì giyud mahuman
ang ímung trabáhu ug maglapyat ka,</i> Your
work will never get done if you work slow.

<b>lapyù</b> <i>a</i> @young and @tender. <i>Ang lapyung bágu
mauy maáyung utánun,</i> Young and tender
<i>bágu</i> leaves make an excellent vegetable
stew. <i>Lapyù nga kaisípan,</i> Young and tender
minds.

<b>lárag</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B2] for leaves to yellow. <i>Nagkalarag
ang mga tanum kay way ulan,</i> The
plants are becoming yellow because there
hasn't been any rain. <b>1a</b> [B12] for leaves or
flowers to wither and fall off. <i>Nalárag ang
mga dáhun sa lawus nga kamunggay,</i> The
withered kamunggay leaves dropped off. <b>2</b>
[B12] be faded. <i>Nalárag na ang íyang kaanyag,</i>
Her beauty has faded. <b>2a</b> <b>-- ang búlak,
pagkabúlak</b> lose one's virginity (for the
flower to fade). <i>Nalárag ang íyang pagkabúlak
sa dihang gipaangkan siya,</i> She lost her
chaste beauty when she became pregnant. <b>3</b>
[B] get completely drunk. <i>Sa ílang pag-ínum
gabíi si Tunyu ang únang nalárag,</i> In
their spree last night Tonio was the first
one to get under the table. <b>3a</b> [B12; a1] be
fascinated with s.o. <i>Ang íyang kaanyag mauy
nakalárag (nakapalárag) nákù,</i> Her beauty
fascinated me. <b>(->)</b> <i>a</i> withered, yellowed
leaves, flowers, faded beauty, unchaste. <i>Gipangasáwa
siya bísan usa na siya ka larag
nga búlak,</i> S.o. married her even though she
was a faded flower (no longer a virgin). <i>n</i>
fallen leaves.

<b>láran</b> <i>v</i> [A12; a12] @beat, @outdo. <i>Dakù túud
si Klí apan walà siya makaláran ni Prísir,</i>
Clay may be big but he couldn't beat Frazier.
<b>pa-</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A3] allow oneself to be outdone.
<b>2</b> [A13] allow oneself to get carried
away with his emotions. <i>Magpaláran ka gánis
ímung kaguul, masakit ka giyud,</i> If you
allow yourself to get carried away with
your emotions, you will surely get sick.

<b>lárang</b> <i>v</i> [A; c1] <b>1</b> stew s.t. with coconut
milk and nothing else but spices. <i>Lamì ang
kyampaw ug ilárang (larángun),</i> The best
way to cook ray is by stewing it in coconut
juice. <b>2</b> reheat s.t. to remove the fat.
<i>Laránga ang adúbu arun dílì kaáyu ngilngig,</i>
Heat the <i>adúbu</i> so it won't be so greasy. <i>n</i>
dish stewed in coconut milk, usually stingray.

<b>láras</b> <i>v</i> [A; b6] @saw along the length. <i>Larásun
nátù ang átung giputul nga káhuy,</i> We'll
saw the log into lumber. <b>(->)</b> <i>v</i> [A; c1] <b>1</b> do
s.t. to all of a group. <i>Ang huramintádu nga
milaras ug patay sa tibuuk pamilya,</i> The
amok who killed all the members of the
family. <i>Ayaw mi larasa (ilaras) ug kasábà
kay usa ray nakasâ[** ^?],</i> Don't include us all in
the scolding because only one of us did
anything wrong. <i>Gilaras ku pagsuruysúruy
ang mga dálan dinhi,</i> I wandered through
all of the streets. <b>2</b> do s.t. to a larger number
of a group than would ordinarily be expected.
<i>Gilaras níyag pangulitáwu ang duha
ka magsúun,</i> He courted two of the sisters
at the same time. <i>n</i> ripsaw, saw for cutting
with the grain. <b>-an(->)</b> <i>n</i> sawhorse. <b>-in-</b> <i>n</i>
boards sawed off with a ripsaw.

<b>láraw</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; ab] @{make plans} to do s.t. <i>Nagláraw
ang prisidinti nga magdiktadur,</i> The
president is planning to become a dictator.
<i>Dúna siyay gilárawng buhátun nímu,</i> He is
plotting to do s.t. against you. <i>Ikay gilaráwan
níyang patyun,</i> He is planning to kill
you. <b>2</b> [A; a2] plan how and where s.t. is
to be built. <i>Magláraw ta sa átung balayan,</i>
We're going to map out the place where the
house is to be built. <i>n</i> plan, plot. <i>Wà kuy láraw
sa pagbiyáhi,</i> I have no plans to travel.
<b>-an</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> picture. <b>2</b> graven image (Biblical).
<i>Dílì ka magsimba sa mga laráwan,</i> Thou
shalt not worship graven images. <b>3</b> image,
likeness of. <i>Laráwan ka sa ímung inahan,</i>
You are your mother's image. <b>4</b> typical example.
<i>Laráwan sa kakúgi ug kabuútan,</i> Paragon
of industry and virtue. <i>Laráwan sa kahimsug,</i>
A picture of health. <i>v</i> [A; a] showing
clearly, picture s.t. <i>Ang ílang kahimtang
naglaráwan sa túmang kakabus,</i> The condition
shows what utter poverty is. <i>Nalaráwan</i>

<b>larga</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B36] for a passenger vehicle to
leave. <i>Milarga (nalarga) ang trák binyáan
ang kunduktur,</i> The bus went off, leaving
the conductor behind. <b>1a</b> leave for a distant
place. <i>Mularga mi ugmà pára Butwan,</i> We'll
leave for Butuan tomorrow. <i>Ug malarga na

we have gotten off. <b>1b</b> used in commands
only: go ahead, start. <i>Ug muingun kung
'larga', dágan ... Na, larga na,</i> When I say
'OK', run ... OK, run! <b>-- manuk</b> = <sc>LARGA</sc>,
<i>1b.</i> <b>3</b>[**typo: 2, image is smudged, or manually proofread] [A3P; b] allow, permit s.o. to do
s.t. freely. <i>Kinsa may naglarga nímu nga ipatandug

free hand to touch that work? <b>2a</b> [A; b]
meet a price offered, agree to do s.t. for a

I'll let it go for twenty. <b>3</b> [A; b7]
pay out the line. <i>Ayaw palabii ug larga sa
tugut ang tabánug,</i> Don't pay out the string

Pay out the fishline. <b>4</b> [A; bc] let cocks go

manuk, súgud na ang búlang,</i> When those
two cocks are released, that means the game

<b>larut</b> <i>v</i> [A3P; a] <b>1</b> @{pull up} by the roots. <i>Maglarut

<b>laslas</b> <i>v</i> [A; a] @cut s.t. with a sawing motion

<b>lasmu</b> <i>a</i> having the fishy odor of stagnant water
or a body of a person who has not bathed
in weeks. <i>Lasmu kaáyu ang kabù kay
walà kahugási,</i> The dipper smells bad because
it hasn't been washed. <i>Lasmu kaáyu
ang isdà sa batu,</i> Fishes that live in rocks

without making a fuss or bother (colloquial).
<i>Wà giyud nay lasmung amahána. Muhátag
dáyun bísag unsay pangayúun sa anak,</i> That
father never makes a fuss. Whatever his son
asks for he gets. <i>v</i> [B; b6] smell fishy or revolting
like stagnant water. <i>Mulasmu ang
plátung dì sabunan inighugas,</i> Plates develop
a fishy smell if you don't wash them
with soap.

<i>n</i> a slender thread which, in folk belief, attaches

(<i>matris</i>) s.w. in the vicinity of the umbilical

<b>ligtak</b> <i>v</i> [B26C; a12P] for the skull to crack.

<b>linga, línga</b> (from <i>alinga</i>) <i>a</i> inattentive due
to preoccupation with s.t. else. <i>Balikbalíka
pag-isplikar kay linga kaáyu,</i> Repeat your
explanation because he is very inattentive.
<i>n</i> preoccupation that keeps one from concentrating.
<i>Dì siya makatrabáhu kay daghan
siyag linga,</i> He can't do work because he has

be inattentive. <i>Wà kung kabantay
pag-ági níya. Nalinga lang ku,</i> I didn't see
her go by. I wasn't paying attention. <i>Subrang
dúwà ang nalingahan ánang batáa,</i>
The child has nothing but play on his mind
and thus is inattentive. <b>2</b> [A12; a] hold
one's attention. <i>Nalinga kug tan-aw sa lamígas
nga nanag-áway,</i> I was amused watching
the ants fighting each other. <i>Lingaha ang
gwardiya kay muipsut ku sa píkas,</i> Keep
the guard occupied because I will slip
through the other side. <b>3</b> [B1256] be so
occupied. <i>Ang tindíra nalinga ug paninsíyu,</i>
The salesgirl was so busy she couldn't make
change properly. <b>maka-r-(<-)</b> <i>a</i> being easily
diverted, distracted. <i>Pangidad nga makalilínga,</i>
Age at which one has a short attention
span.

<b>lubat</b> <i>n</i> illness caused by a frightening experience,

for an illness to develop or for s.t.
that one has to get worse because of intense

cemetery when you have them. <i>Gilubatan
ang bátà kay gidúul sa minatay,</i> The child
got ill from fright because he was made to
go near the corpse. <b>pa-</b> <i>v</i> [A; c] startle s.o.
by s.t. sudden--a shout or a sudden spring

ang pultahan nga gikalit pagsira,</i> The
door was slammed with a bang. <i>Naglugapak
ang samput sa íyang anak sa bakus,</i> The
leather belt cracked over his son's buttocks.
<b>-in-</b> = <sc>LUGÁPAK</sc>, <i>n</i>.

<b>lugar_{1}</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> geographical place. <i>Nakaadtu na</i>
-----File: 1295.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>ku sa lainláing lugar sa kalibútan,</i> I have
been to various places in the world. <b>1a</b> situation
one is in. <i>Ikaw sa ákung lugar ug lalim
ba,</i> You try being in my place and see
if it is nice. <b>2</b> proper place, occasion for s.t.
<i>Ibutang sa lugar ang ímung pagpangmik-ap,</i>
Use make-up at the proper occasion. <i>Walà
sa lugar tung ímung pagsaway níya kay daghang
namínaw,</i> It was not the right time for
you to criticise him because there were lots
of people listening. <b>2a</b> proper place of vehicles
in the flow of traffic. <i>Patuu. Wà ka sa
lugar,</i> Move to the right. You're not in your
lane. <b>3</b> vacant place. <i>Dùna[**typo: Dúna] pa bay lugar sa
dyíp?</i> Is there room in the jeep? <b>4</b> available
time for s.t. <i>Wà kuy lugar pagsúruy
run,</i> I don't have time to go around now. <b>5</b>
@chance or @opportunity to do s.t. <i>Way lugar
pagdúul níya kay gwardiyádu,</i> There is no
chance to get near him because he is guarded.
<b>6</b> <b>primíru (ikaduha,</b> etc.) -- in the first
(second, etc.) @place. <i>Ayawg adtu. Primíru
lugar istranyu ka,</i> Don't go there. In the
first place, you are a stranger. <b>lugráha, lugaráha</b>
<i>n</i> particular place, time, chance. <i>v</i> <b>1</b>
[A; b(1)] @{give way} or space to. <i>Milugar siya
arun makalingkud ang babáyi,</i> He gave
his place so the lady could sit. <i>Lugari ang
Prisidinti inigsúut níya sa nanambung,</i> Give
way to the President when he goes through
the crowd. <b>2</b> [A3; b(1)] give the chance to
do s.t. <i>Musabut giyug íyang pápa kay mulugar
man inigpamisíta nákù,</i> Her father is
sure understanding because he leaves us
alone (lit. gives a chance) when I go visiting.
<i>Ayaw siyag lugari nga muantug,</i> Don't give
him the chance to shoot the ball. <b>3</b> [A12]
<b>3a</b> get a chance to do s.t. <i>Hagki dáyun siya
ug makalugar ka,</i> Kiss her as soon as you
get the chance. <b>3b</b> have the time to. <i>Buháta
ni ug makalugar ka,</i> Do this if you have the
time to. <b>4</b> [A2; c6] pull over in a place
proper for stopping a vehicle. <i>Ilugar ang
dyip ug muhúnung ka,</i> Pull over to the
side of the road when you stop. <i>a</i> <b>1</b> having
available space. <i>Kargáhi pa kay lugar pa kaáyu,</i>
Put in more passengers because there's
still plenty of space. <b>2</b> for there to be a
chance. <i>Dì ku mangupya bísag lugar kaáyu,</i>
I won't cheat even if I have a good chance
to do so. <b>pa-</b> <i>v</i> [A; b(1)] give s.o. a chance
to come near or touch one. <i>Di[typo: Dì] nà siya magbinúang
bísag palugaran,</i> He won't do anything
foolish even if given the chance. <b>tag-</b>
<i>n</i> spirit inhabiting a particular place. <i>Gidaútan
nà siya sa taglugar kay íyang giputul
ang káhuy,</i> The spirit of the place made him
ill when he cut the tree down.
-----File: 1296.png--------------------------------------------------------

<b>lugar_{2}</b> = <sc>KINTA_{1}</sc>.

<b>lugas</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> @grain. <i>Usa ka lugas humay,</i> A grain
of rice. <i>Maáyu ang lugas sa igtalánum nga
binhì,</i> The seeds for planting have well-formed
grains. <b>1a</b> @drops (figurative). <i>Pipila
ka lugas nga lúhà,</i> A few teardrops. <b>2</b> strand.
<i>Usa ka lugas buhuk,</i> A strand of hair. <b>2a</b> <b>--
lánut</b> a hair's breadth (lit. strand of abaca
fiber) by which one is kept from death. <i>Usa
ka lugas lánut ang nakauwang nákù sa kamatáyun,</i>
I came within a hair's breadth of
meeting my death. <b>3</b> word counter for people.
<i>Pipila ka lugas táwu ang didtu sa sinihan,</i>
There were only a few people in the
movies. <b>4</b> word counter for things which
can be counted but not concrete. <i>Pipila ka
lugas púlung,</i> A few words. <i>Pipila ka lugas
kanta,</i> A few songs. <i>Pipila ka lugas idíya,</i> A
few ideas.

<b>lug-as</b> <i>v</i> [B12; a12] remove husk from rice
or other grains. <i>Ang ímung linubkan dì makalug-as
(makapalug-as) sa dáwa,</i> The way
you are doing it won't get the husks off the
millet. <i>a</i> already unhusked. <i>Taphi ang linubuk
kay lug-as na,</i> Winnow the pounded
rice because the husks are off now.

<b>lugátub</b> <i>n</i> deep, loud, hollow sound. <i>v</i> [A] resound
with a deep loud, hollow sound. <i>Milugátub
ang baril nga gilábayg batu,</i> The
barrel went bonk when a stone was thrown
at it. <b>-in-</b> = <sc>LUGÁTUB</sc>.

<b>lúgaw</b> <i>n</i> @porridge from rice or corn grits. <i>v</i> <b>1</b>
[A; a] make porridge. <i>Bag-ung humay ang
lugáwa,</i> Make porridge from the new rice. <b>2</b>
[B12] turn to, become a mud puddle or

path becomes slush during rainy days. <b>-in-,
ni-</b> <i>n</i> = <sc>LÚGAW</sc>.

<b>*lugay-nan, -nun</b> <i>n</i> pertaining to politics and
elections. <i>Bugnù nga lugaynun (lugaynan)
diin napárut si Kirínu,</i> The political fight
where Quirino lost.

<b>lugbak</b> <i>v</i> [B26] for organic matter to decay.
<i>Malugbak ang prútas nga may tatsa,</i> The
fruit will @rot if it has been damaged. <i>Bisan
malugbak ang ímung bukug, dílì ka kabalus
sa ímung ginikánan,</i> You can never repay
your parents no matter how much time goes
by (lit. even after your bones have rotted).
<i>Mauy nakalugbak (nakapalugbak) sa káhuyng
halígi ang kanúnayng paghúmul níini
sa túbig,</i> The wooden post rotted because
it was immersed too long in water.

<b>lugdang</b> <i>v</i> [A2; b6] <b>1</b> settle to the bottom of

for results of bad action to make themselves

<b>lugdat</b> <i>v</i> [B46] for the eyes to bulge. <i>Milugdat
ang íyang mata sa katingála,</i> Her eyes

<b>lugdum</b>, <b>lugdung</b> <i>a</i> heavily @overcast, particularly

<b>lúgì_{1}</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; a] extract dried coconut meat

<b>(->)</b> <i>n</i> instrument for extracting coconut

<b>lúgì_{2}</b> <i>a</i> being outsmarted, fooled (slang). <i>Lúgì

[A; a2b3(1)] defeat in a game or fight. <i>Ang
manghud ra nákuy maglúgí níya sa ahidris,</i>
Even my little brother could defeat him in
chess. <i>Ang liphuk ni Prasyir mauy nalugian

<b>lugtas</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; a] break a rope, thread, string,

@finish a task or job. <i>Kanang labhanan na

<b>ma-_{1}</b> future verb affix. (<i>Past</i>: <b>na-</b>. <i>Subjunctive</i>:
<b>ma-</b>.) <b>1</b> potential of the direct passive.
(<i>See</i> <b>-un_{1}</b> for meanings of the direct passive.
See <i>maka-</i> for meanings of the potential.)
<i>Mapalit nà nímu bísag ása,</i> You can buy
that anywhere. <i>Wà ku pa mabása,</i> I haven't
had a chance to read it. <i>Uy! Dì man diay</i>
-----File: 1350.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>ákù ning nadá nákung pitáka,</i> Heavens, I
took s.o. else's purse by mistake. <b>2</b> potential
of the instrumental passive. (See <i>i-_{1}</i> for
meanings of the instrumental passive.) <i>Dì ni
mabaligyà kay mahal da kaáyu ang prisyu,</i>
You can't sell this because it's too expensive.
<i>Wà pa nákù mahátag níya kay wà pa siya
muabut,</i> I haven't had a chance to give
it to him because he hasn't arrived. <i>Halá!
Nabungat ra ba nákù ang sikrítu,</i> Oh God!
I let out the secret. <b>3</b> <i>active of stative verbs</i>:
may become [so-and-so]. <i>Ayaw nag hikápa.
Magubà unyà nà,</i> Don't touch that. It
might break. <i>Ilhan nga mulubad nang panaptúna
ug mapula ang túbig,</i> You'll know
the cloth runs if the water turns red. <i>Nawálà
ang ákung singsing,</i> My ring got lost. <b>3a</b>
<i>with roots that refer to nonvolitional actions</i>:
[do]. <i>Matingála siya ug ngánu tu,</i> He
will be amazed at why it should be so. <i>Wà
ku mabaláka,</i> I am not worried. <i>Mah[=ú]g unyà
ka ug mabálì ang sanga,</i> You will fall if
the branch breaks. <i>Ug matúlug na sila,</i>
When they are asleep. <i>Mahadluk ku,</i> I am
afraid. <i>Dì ka ba malúuy níya?</i> Don't you
feel sorry for him? <b>3b</b> <i>with nouns</i>: become
[so-and-so]. <i>Ug maduktur ka na,</i> When you
get to be a doctor. <b>3c</b> <i>with nouns which refer
to a place</i>: wind up in [such-and-such]
a place. <i>Malangit kag maimpirnu ba?</i> Will
you go to heaven or will you go to hell?
<i>Mauspital giyud kag pasagdan lang nà nímung
sakíta,</i> You'll end up in the hospital
if you let your sickness go. <b>3d</b> with nouns
referring to time: get to be [such-and-such]
a time. Ug maalas tris na gánì, mulakaw na
ku, If it gets to be three o'clock, I'll leave.
Ug magabíi nag wà pa siya, If it gets to be
nightfall and he hasn't arrived. <b>3e</b> (only
with the future) when [such-and-such] a
time or season comes about. <i>Magkítà ra silag
mapista,</i> They only see each other during
fiestas. <i>Tábù dinhi ug maduminggu,</i>
They hold market here on Sundays.

<b>ma-_{2}</b> <b>1</b> affix added to most adjective roots
which do not refer to a measurement to
form adjectives which mean 'very [so-and-so]'.
This formation is used in literary or
formal styles. <i>Usa ka mapait nga pahíyum,</i>
A very bitter smile. <b>2</b> added to some verbs
to form adjectives meaning [do]ing, usually
with a short penult. <i>Bátang mahilak,</i> A
crybaby. <i>Matulug,</i> Of a sleepy sort. <i>Matawa,</i>
Full of laughter.

<b>ma-ánun</b> alternant of <i>ma-un</i>, used with some
bases in place of <i>ma-un</i>. <i>Masuk-ánun,</i> Tending
to get irritated.

<b>máas</b> <i>a</i> @old, @aged. <i>Bisan máas na siya tisar gi-*</i>
-----File: 1351.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>*hápung mulakaw,</i> He may be old, but he
still walks erect. <i>v</i> [B] @{become old}. <i>Kun
mumáas na ang kalbásà dílì na maútan,</i>
When a squash becomes too old, it is no
longer good to eat.

<b>mabà</b> = <sc>MUBÙ</sc>.

<b>mabaw</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> @shallow. <i>Mabaw ra kaáyu nang ímung
pangatarúngan,</i> Your reasoning is very
shallow. <i>Dì kalanguyan nang subáa kay mabaw,</i>
You can't swim in that river. It's too
shallow. <i>Ang baskit nga mabaw ug lubut diyútayg
sulud,</i> A shallow basket holds little.
<i>Mabaw nga panaksan,</i> Shallow bowl. <b>2</b> <i>in
set expressions</i>: <b>-- ug lubut</b> @sensitive or
quick to anger. <i>Muhílak diay bísag kumidiya
ra. Kamabaw nímug lubut uy,</i> Why did
you cry when it was just a joke? How sensitive
you are! <b>3</b> <b>-- ug salabútan</b> @unintelligent.
<i>Dúgay siyang kasabut kay mabaw rag
salabútan,</i> She doesn't understand readily
because she is unintelligent. <i>v</i> [B; b7c1]
become shallow. <i>Imabaw (mabwa) lang pagkálut
ang tamnan ug kamúti,</i> Just make the
hole for the sweet potatoes shallow. <b>hi-/ha-(->)</b>
<i>see</i> <sc>HIMÁBAW</sc> <i>under</i> <sc>BABAW</sc>. <b>-g-</b> shallow
(plural). <b>i-</b> n place above s.t. <i>Imabaw sa
kaban nákù gibutang ang libru,</i> I put the

do in a shallow way. <i>Kun minagbáwun
lang ni nátù pagsabut ang giisplikar sa maistru,
dílì giyud ta makapasar,</i> If you fail to
understand (lit. understand shallowly) what
the teacher explained, you won't pass. <b>ka-(<-)</b>
n half brother, sister. <i>Kamábaw ku siya
kay paríhu mig inahan,</i> He is my half brother
because we have the same mother. <i>v</i> [A23]
be half brothers, sisters.

<b>mabdus</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> @pregnant. <b>2</b> for rice grains to be
in the panicle. <i>Mabdus na ang humay,</i> The
rice grains are forming. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B26] get, make
pregnant. <i>Mimabdus si Maríya kay hagithagitun
kaáyu,</i> Maria got pregnant because she
was flirtatious. <b>1a</b> [A1; c] carry in the
womb. <i>Gimabdus nà siya pagkamatay sa íyang
amahan,</i> He was in his mother's womb
when his father died. <b>2</b> [B] for rice grains
to form in the panicle. <b>3</b> [B1] for borrowed
things to have been kept too long. <i>Dúgay
kaáyu nímung giúlì ang ákung libru. Mimabdus
na nà,</i> You kept my book too long (lit.
so long that it got pregnant). <b>4</b> [B1] <b>-- sa
pasálig</b> get fooled by assurances (lit. got
pregnant because of promises). <i>Daghan nang
mimabdus sa pasálig sa mga pulitiku,</i> Many
people have been fooled by the politician's
assurances. <b>pa-</b> <i>v</i> [A; c2] get s.o. pregnant.
<i>Gipamabdus (gipamabdúsan) si Maríya ni</i>

<i>Pidru</i>, Pedro got Maria pregnant.

<b>mabgas</b> = <sc>MALUBGAS</sc>.

<b>mabúlu</b> <i>n</i> k.o. medium-sized tree of the primary

<b>madri míya</b> an exclamation of alarm, surprise,

tingálig mah[=ú]g nang bátà,</i> My God! Watch
out, the baby is going to fall. <i>Madri míya!

did that!

<b>mag-</b> durative active verbal affix, future.
(<i>Past</i>: <b>nag-</b> <i>or</i> <b>ga-</b>. <i>Subjunctive</i>: <b>mag-</b>.) <i>Magmata
sila árung urása,</i> They are awake at
this time. <i>Nagmata (or gamata) pa ba kahà
sila,[** , should be: ?]</i> Do you think they are still awake? <i>Walà
na sila magmata,</i> They are not awake any
more. Verbs with <i>mag-</i>, <i>nag-</i> have the following
meanings (as opposed to verbs with
<i>mi-</i>, <i>mu-</i> -- <i>see</i> <sc>MU-</sc>): <sc>1</sc> action not necessarily
intentional. <i>Walà siya magsulti,</i> He
didn't say. <i>Walà ku maghátag níya ánang
librúha,</i> I didn't give him that book. <sc>2</sc> durative
action, action or state continuing in
time. <i>Wà na siya maghilak,</i> He isn't crying
any more. <i>Ug magtindug ang mga táwu sa
atubángan, dì mi makakità,</i> If the people in
front are standing, we won't be able to see.
<sc>2a</sc> added to nouns. <i>Ug magkalayu na ang
kakugnan háyag kaáyu ang lángit,</i> When the
fields are ablaze, the skies light up. <i>Human
sa púlù ka gutlù, ang puthaw magbaga,</i> After
ten seconds the steel will glow. <sc>3</sc> <i>added
to verbs referring to a state</i>: be in [such-and-such]
a state. <i>Ug mag-abri ang pultahan,
musulud giyud ang lángaw,</i> If the door
is open, the flies are sure to come in. <i>Walà
na magtuyuk ang ligid,</i> The wheel is no
longer turning. <sc>3a</sc> <i>added to adjectives</i>: be
[adj.]. <i>Magmalipáyun ta,</i> Let us be happy.
<i>Mawà kay hitsúra ug magpula nang ímung
nawung,</i> You will not look good if your
face is all red. <sc>3b</sc> added to words referring
to a state of the weather. <i>Atúa giyud siya sa
dágat, magbálud kinig maglínaw,</i> He is at sea,
whether it is wavy or calm. <i>Mag-ulan kag
mag-ínit,</i> Rain or shine (lit. whether you are
rainy or shining). <sc>4</sc> <i>referring to an action
which redounded on the agent</i>: do [so-and-so]
to oneself. Mag-ílis pa ku, I will change
my clothes. <i>Gustu kung maglumus,</i> I want
to drown myself. <sc>4a</sc> <i>added</i> to nouns: become
a [so-and-so]. <i>Magpárì ku,</i> I will become
a priest. <i>Magsirkadur tingáli ning bataána,</i>
This child probably wants to become
a trapeze artist. <sc>5</sc> referring to an action
which two or more people did with each
other. (Verbs with <i>mag-</i> of this sort always
have penultimate stress.) <i>Didtu sila mag-ábut,</i>
They met in that place. <i>Magsákay ta,</i>
-----File: 1354.png--------------------------------------------------------
Let us ride together. <i>Ug maglagyù pagkabutang
ang mga balay,</i> If the houses are far
apart from one another. <b>5a</b> <i>with nouns</i>: be
in the [noun] relation. <i>Magkumpári kami
ug akuy pakugúsun sa íyang anak,</i> We will
be <i>kumpári's</i> if I become his child's god-*father.
<i>Mag-amígu lang ta,</i> Let's be friends.

<b>maga-</b> alternative form for <i>mag-</i> in meanings
<i>2</i>, <i>2a</i>, <i>3</i>, <i>3a</i>, <i>4</i>. Words with <i>maga-</i> can substitute
for the examples there given.

<b>Magahat</b> <i>n</i> pagan non-Cebuano peoples in
the mountains (applies to pagans in Negros
and in Mindanao). <i>v</i> [A13] be very touchy.
<i>Ug napildi ka ug dakù magmagahat diay ka?</i>
You are touchy just because you lost heavily?

<b>magalyánis</b> <i>n</i> downtown shopping district of
Cebu (after the name of Magallanes Street,
which formerly was the principal shopping
street in Cebu).

<b>magang</b>, <b>mágang</b> <i>v</i> [BN] for corn to flower.
<i>Inigmagang sa mais, mugítib na ang lugas,</i>
When the corn flowers, the grains begin to
develop.

<b>magasin_{1}</b> <i>n</i> @magazine, @periodical.

<b>magasin_{2}</b> <i>n</i> @{ammunition clip} for automatic
firearms.

<b>magay</b> <i>n</i> @maguey, cultivated as a source of

[A] make into sisal hemp. <b>magay mágay</b> <i>n</i>
ornamental plant similar to the maguey but
smaller in size: <b><i>Sansevieria spp.</i></b>

<b>magaya</b> = <sc>MALAGAYA</sc>.

Magindánaw <i>n</i> @Muslims of Cotabato and
Zamboanga del Sur.

<b>magka-</b> <i>durative active future for verbs referring
to a state</i>: be, becoming more and
more [so-and-so]. (<i>Past</i>: <b>nagka-</b>. <i>Subjunctive</i>:
<b>magka-</b>.) Verbs with this affix always
have a stressed final syllable. <i>Imbis nga magkakusug,
nagkahinay hinúun,</i> Instead of getting
faster and faster, it was getting slower
and slower. <i>Wà lagi magkaduul ang bapur
nganhi, nagkalayù hinúun,</i> The boat is not
coming nearer. It's actually getting further
and further away.

<b>magka-(<-)</b> potential active verb affix, future.
(Past: <b>nagka-</b>. Subjunctive: <b>magka-</b>.)
Used with verbs referring to mutual actions
(cf. <i>mag-_{1}</i>, <i>5</i>) but otherwise paralleling the
potential meanings listed under <i>maka-</i>. <b>1</b>
can [do] with each other. <i>Dì tang tanan
magkasákay,</i> We cannot all ride together. <b>2</b>
manage to [do] with each other. <i>Wà mi
magkasábut,</i> We didn't manage to come to
an agreement. <i>Nagkaábut sila sa tungàtúngà,</i>
They met in the middle. <b>3</b> happen to [do]
with each other. <i>Ug magkakítà gánì ang</i>
-----File: 1355.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>ímung babáyig asáwa,</i> If your mistress and
your wife happen to run into each other.

<b>mag-l-</b> alternant of <i>mag-r-</i>, and usually in
competition with it, but with some roots
only <i>mag-r-</i> is frequent or the form with
<i>mag-r-</i> has acquired a different nuance. <i>Magbalantay,</i>
Watchman. <i>Magbuluhat ug mga
mwiblis,</i> Furniture maker.

<b>maglalatik</b> <i>n</i> k.o. folk dance in which half
coconut shells are knocked to the rhythm
of the accompanying music.

<b>magnisya</b> <i>n</i> @{milk of magnesia}. <b>-- simpli</b> a half
dose of milk of magnesia (as opposed to <i>--

<b>magnit</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> @magnet. <b>2</b> kissing scene (slang--from
the notion that the faces come together
as if magnetized). <i>Daghang magnit
ánang salidáha,</i> There are plenty of kissing

(slang). <i>a</i> won over. <i>Inigkanta nímu, magnit
na silang tanan,</i> When you sing, they'll all
be won over.

<b>mag-r-</b> <i>n</i> prefix added to verbs to form nouns
which refer to one who does [verb] on a
regular basis. <i>Magbabantay</i>, Watchman.
<i>Magsusúlat</i>, Writer. Magpapatigayun, Businessman.
<i>Magyuyutà</i>, Landowner or farmer.
<i>Magbubúhat</i>, The Creator (God) or
one who does.

<b>mahal</b> <i>a</i> <b>1</b> @dear, @expensive. <i>Mahal na kaáyu

<b>mahan</b> = <sc>MAN KAHÀ</sc> (dialectal). <i>see</i> <sc>MAN</sc>.

<b>maharlika</b> <i>n</i> the name given to the native

<b>máhay</b> <i>n</i> feelings of hurt and @regret at what

who attack on s.o. are beaten up instead
(i.e., they cannot blame anyone but themselves),
and when people who set on s.o.
are unsuccessful (i.e., no one felt bad because
they were successful).

taste to <i>lungbuy</i>: <b><i>Eugenia polycephaloides</i></b>.

<b>maka-_{1}</b> potential active verb affix, future.
(<i>Past</i>: <b>naka-</b>. <i>Subjunctive</i>: <b>maka-</b>. <i>Short
form</i>: <b>ka-</b>.) <i>Dì ku makaalsa (kaalsa) niánà,</i>
I cannot lift that. <i>Nakatilaw (katilaw) na ku
niánà,</i> I have tried that. <i>Wà ku makasakay
(kasakay),</i> I couldn't get a ride. <b>1</b> refers to
an action s.o. has the capability of doing.
(Only the future form is used in this meaning.)
<i>Makamau na kung mukinatsilà sa nag-idad
kug diyis,</i> I knew how to speak Spanish
when I was ten years old. <b>2</b> refers to an action
which one had the opportunity or
managed to do. <i>Ug makaadtu ku sa inyu
human sa paniudtu, muhapit ku,</i> If I get a
chance to go to your place after lunch, I'll
drop in. <i>Wà ku makalakaw kay síging abut
ang mga bisíta,</i> I didn't have a chance to go
out because we kept having visitors. <b>2a</b> <i>with
nouns</i>: manage to get. <i>Ug trís ákung mahulbut
run, makamadyung ku,</i> If I draw a three,
I will get mahjong. <i>Niíning trabahúa hálus
ta makasininà,</i> With this work I can hardly
earn enough to buy a shirt. <b>3</b> refers to an
accidental or unintentional action. <i>Diriyut
siya makaihì sa dihang gilatigu siya sa íyang</i>
-----File: 1358.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>inahan,</i> Her mother whipped her so hard
she nearly wet her pants. <i>Makaingun kag
nindut ug makakità ka,</i> Once you see it,
you won't be able to help exclaiming at
how beautiful it is.

<b>maka-_{2}</b> <i>short form</i>: <b>ka-_{4}</b> <i>n</i> affix added to
numbers to form words which mean [do
so-and-so] many times. <i>Makapila (kapila)
ku na ikaw ingna?</i> How many times did I
tell you? <i>Makaduha na ku malígù didtu,</i> I
have gone swimming there twice. <i>Makadaghan
na ku mabiktima,</i> I have been victimized
many times.

<b>makalibri</b> = <sc>KALIBRI_{2}</sc>.

<b>2</b> k.o. very fat pig. <i>a</i> @obese. <i>Gwapahun untang
bayhána apan makan lang,</i> She's quite
beautiful, only she's fat.

<b>makapunù</b> (from <i>punù</i>) <i>n</i> variety of coconut
which produces ordinary fruit and once in
a while fruit which are completely full of
soft meat, slightly harder near the shell.
The <i>makapunù</i> fruit is highly esteemed and
is used for sweets.

<b>maka-r-</b> affix added to verbs referring to a
state to form adjectives which mean cause
s.o. to get into [such-and-such] a state to a
great extent. Forms with this affix usually
have long penults. <i>Makasusúbung hitabù,</i> A
very saddening event. <i>Makalulúuy</i>, Inspiring
pity. <i>Makalalagut</i>, Angering.

<b>makarúni</b> <i>n</i> @macaroni. <i>v</i> [A13] cook a macaroni
dish.

immigrated from Macao). <b>lútung --</b> <i>see</i>
<sc>LÚTÙ</sc>.

<b>máki_{1}</b> <i>n</i> a large, enamel-coated, round, metal

cooked rice or corn.

<b>máki_{2}</b> <i>n</i> a Chinese dish of sliced meats,
stewed and thickened with cornstarch.

<b>makig-(<-)</b> prefix added to bases with a prefix
<i>pakig-</i> to indicate future, volitional active
forms. <i>Past</i>: <b>nakig-</b>. <i>Subjunctive</i>: <b>makig-</b>.
No durative or potential forms. (<i>See</i>
<sc>PAKIG-</sc> <i>for meanings</i>.) <i>Short forms</i>: <b>kig-</b> and
<b>tig-</b>. <i>Makigkáun (kigkáun, tigkáun) siya nákù
sa gawas,</i> He wants to take me out to eat.
<i>Nakig-áway siyag dakung táwu,</i> He picked
a fight with a large person. <i>Walà ku makigpustaánay
níya,</i> I did not challenge him to
bet.

<b>man 1</b> because. <i>Kay ang íya dapit man sa dáhun,
mamúnga dáyun,</i> Because his part was
the part with the leaves, it would bear fruit
quickly. <b>-- ugud</b> because (giving an explanation).
<i>Namatay ang tanum kay wà man gud
bùbúi,</i> The plant died because no one watered
it. <b>2</b> <i>after an interrogative:</i> particle to
make the question not abrupt. <i>Háin man si-*</i>
-----File: 1366.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>*ya?</i> Could you tell me where he is? <b>3</b> particle
with a statement contradicting a previous
statement or presumption. <i>Dì man nà
mau,</i> That's not the one. <b>4</b> particle with a
statement giving information. <i>Nía man si
Pidru karung buntága,</i> Oh, Pedro is here
this morning. <b>-- diay</b> I notice that. <i>Nindut
man diay ka kaáyung mukanta!</i> Oh, I see
you sing very beautifully. <b>-- kahà</b> [so-and-so]
apparently is the case. <i>Kami man kahay
muluhud, anus-a man ang kasal?</i> We are
supposed to sponsor you, so when is the
wedding going to be? <i>Dì lang ka tagáan. Dì
man kahà ka gustu,</i> I won't give you any.
You apparently won't want any, anyway.
<b>-- lagi</b> I notice [so-and-so] is the case, nevertheless.
<i>Ingun siya dì ka muanhi. Nía ka
man lagi,</i> He said you weren't coming, but
here you are! <b>5</b> in other phrases: <b>ingun --</b>
as well as. <i>Mubuhis ang tagasyudad ingun
man ang tagabaryu,</i> The city people, as well
as the barrio folks, pay taxes. <b>mau -- gánì</b>
that's why, despite what you would expect....
<i>Mau man gánì nga namula ang ákung
pánit kay nabulad ku,</i> I have red skin, despite
what you would expect, because I
was out in the sun. <b>na --</b> <i>see</i> <b>NA,</b> <i>4.</i> <b>pála --
run</b> that's flattery. <i>Pála man run ug dì pa tinúud,</i>
That would have been flattery if it
were not true. <b>túud --</b> and so, as one would
expect. <i>Túud man miabut dáyun ang pulis,</i>
And so, as one would expect, the police
immediately arrived.

<b>maN-</b> <i>(see p. xvi for the meaning of the symbol N)</i>
prefix added to bases with a prefix
<b>paN-</b> to indicate future volitional active
forms. <i>(past</i> <b>naN-;</b> <i>subjunctive</i> <b>maN-.</b> <i>Durative
forms: future and subjunctive</i> <b>magpaN-(->);</b>
<i>past</i> <b>nagpaN-(->).</b> <i>Potential active:
future and subjunctive</i> <b>makapaN-;</b> <i>past</i> <b>nakapaN-.)</b>
<i>Mangutána ta kun háin siya,</i> Let us
ask where he is. <i>Wà siya mangutána, He
didn't ask. Nangutána ku piru way tubag,</i> I
asked but there was no answer. <i>Nagpanguput
siya sa kahadluk,</i> He held on with all
his might for fright. <i>Walà ku makapangutána,</i>
I didn't get a chance to ask. <i>Makapangasáwa
ka na,</i> You can get married now.

<b>manga</b> <i>always written</i> <b>mga. 1</b> particle optionally
placed preceding a noun or adjective to
indicate plurals, but referring only to things
that are not all exactly alike. <i>Ang mga istudiyanti
nanambung sa míting,</i> The various
students attended the meeting. <i>Mga karáan
kining mga libru,</i> These are all old books. <b>1a</b>
particle preceding the name for parts of the
body of which there are more than one. <i>Sakit
ákung mga mata,</i> My eyes hurt. <b>2</b> preceding
a form referring to time, measurement:
about, approximately. <i>Mga alas utsu,</i>
At around eight o'clock. <i>Mupalit kug kutsi,
tingáli mga Iníru,</i> I will buy a car, probably
around January. <i>Mga duha ka búwan kanhi,</i>
About two months ago. <i>Mga duha ka pulgáda,</i>
About two inches. <i>Mga dus písus,</i>
Around two pesos.

the ways of the world. <b>2</b> @wise, @tricky. <i>Matríru
ang mga matansíru kay dílì hustu ang
timbangan,</i> The meat sellers are very tricky
because the scales are not honest. <b>3</b> for
game to be shy and not easily approached
by persons. <i>v</i> [B1] be, become wise to the
ways of the world or tricky.

<b>matris_{1}</b> <i>n</i> @uterus.

<b>matris_{2}</b> <i>n</i> @mattress.

<b>matrúna</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> the head @maid in a wealthy
household, the one in charge of running the
household. <b>2</b> @housemother of a women's
dormitory or boarding house. <i>a</i> @matronly-looking,
old, and slightly stout. <i>v</i> [B136; c16]
be, become a house mother or head
maid; get to be @matronly in appearance.

<b>mats</b> <i>v</i> [B; c6] for wearing apparel to match.
<i>Mimats ang ímung sapátus sa pitáka,</i> Your
shoes match your purse.

<b>matsa</b> <i>v</i> [A1; c1] do s.t. in a relaxed and unhurried
manner. <i>Ayaw matsaha (imatsa)
nang ímung linaktan ug sugúun ka,</i> Don't
take it so slow when you are told to do s.t.

<b>matsing_{1}</b> <i>n</i> small monkey. <i>a</i> <b>1</b> like a monkey
in appearance. <b>2</b> @mischievous. <i>Matsing kaáyu
ning batáa u, lukup lag panúngug sa
uban,</i> This child is mischievous. He keeps
on teasing the others. <i>v</i> [B145] look ugly
-----File: 1390.png--------------------------------------------------------
like a monkey. <i>Nagmatsing lang nang dagway
mu,</i> You have a monkey's face.

<b>matsing_{2}</b> <i>n</i> matching type exam.

<b>matsuy</b> humorous euphemism for <sc>MATAY</sc>,
exclamation of displeasure. <i>Matsuy ning batáa,
langas kaáyu,</i> My! What a nuisance this
child is.

<b>mátud</b> [<i>gen.</i>] according to what [so-and-so]
says. <i>Mátud níya, maáyu kanang klási,</i>
According to him that is a good kind. <i>'Adtu
na ta,' mátud níya,</i> He said, 'Let's go.'

<b>matulì</b> <i>n</i> k.o. <i>balat</i> (sea cucumber).

<b>matúmat</b> <i>v</i> [C; bc3] engage in a friendly,
casual chat. <i>Dì ku makigmatúmat nímug
dúgay kay nagdalì ku,</i> I can't chat with you
for long because I'm in a hurry.

<b>matun</b> <i>n</i> @ruffian, @{tough guy}. <i>Daghang istambay
nga matun sa piyir,</i> There are many ruffians
hanging around at the pier. <i>v</i> [B2; b6]
be, become a tough guy.

<b>matutù</b> <i>v</i> [A; a12] <b>1</b> take care of a child.
<i>Kinsay nagmatutù sa ímung anak samtang
walà ka?</i> Who took care of your child when
you were gone? <b>2</b> @rear, @{bring up}. <i>Akuy
nagmatutù kaníla hangtud sa ílang pagkaulitáwu,</i>
I reared the boys until they were
teen-agers. <b>2a</b> [A; b5c] inculcate with s.t.
<i>Matutua (matutui) ang mga tinun-an sa nasyunalismu,</i>
Teach the pupils nationalism. <b>3</b>
nurture a feeling. <i>May gimatutù siyang pagdumut
álang kanákù,</i> He is nursing a grudge
against me. <i>n</i> @care, @guidance. <i>Matutù sa inahan,</i>
Mother's guidance.

<b>matyag</b> <i>v</i> [A; a12b2] @observe, watch to @see.
<i>Siyay mumatyag sa kamaisan nga dì kan-un
sa mga amù,</i> He will watch the cornfield to
see if the monkeys are getting at it. <i>Nakamatyag
ka nag táwung giupirahan?</i> Have
you ever watched a person being operated
on? see also <sc>BATYAG</sc>.

<b>matyanak</b> = <sc>MANTIYÁNAK</sc>.

<b>mau</b> <i>short forms</i>: <b>mu</b>, <b>maw</b> is, are, was, were.
<b>1a</b> preceding subject in sentences with nominal
predicates. <i>Kadtung íyang gisulti mau
ang nakapalágut nákù,</i> What he said was
what angered me. <i>Ang kangihit sa tambal
muy nakapataas sa prisyu,</i> The scarcity of
medicine is what made prices high. <b>1b</b> <i>with
no subject</i>: it's [predicate] which is the
one. <i>Nagtúu giyud aku nga kanà mau,</i> I
believe that that is the one. <i>Ug mau kanà,
ang útang maimpas sunud búlan,</i> If that is
the case, the debt will be paid off next
month. <i>Ang ímung tubag dílì mau,</i> Your
answer is not right. <b>-- bítaw</b> that is so. <i>Kadakung
trabáhu nu? Mau bítaw,</i> What a big
job, isn't it? It certainly is! <b>-- kaáyu</b> the
very one. <i>Mau ni? Mau kaáyu,</i> Is this the
-----File: 1391.png--------------------------------------------------------
one? Yes it is the very one. <b>-- gayud</b> that is
the way it is. <i>Mau giyud nà siya ug mahubug,</i>
That is the way he is when drunk. <b>--
gihápun</b> it's (it was) as usual. <i>Ang atup sa
ámung balay mau gihápun, nípà,</i> The roof
of our house is the usual kind--of palm
thatch. <b>-- lang</b> <i>see</i> <sc>LÁMANG</sc>, <i>2c1</i>. <b>-- kini ug
kini</b>, <b>-- kanà ug kanà</b> <i>in giving excuses, reasons
or alibis</i>: it is because of this, because of
that. <b>1c</b> <i>in response to a question as to the
identification of s.t.</i>: yes, it is the one. <i>Mau
ba ni ang imúha? Dílì mau,</i> Is this yours?
No, that is not the one. <i>Si Pidru na ba nà?
Mau na,</i> Is that Peter now? It's him all
right. <b>1d</b> yes, that is the case, said esp. in
response to negative comments. <i>'Kusug siyang
manghulam mu rag kamaung muúlì.'--'Mau,'</i>
'She likes to borrow things as if
she knew enough to return them (which
she doesn't).'--'Yes, that is so.' <b>1e</b> <b>-- nang</b>,
<b>-- na sa ginháwang [<i>verb</i>]</b> doing one's best,
tiring oneself out doing [verb]. <i>Mau na nga
pangítà nákù, (or mau na sa ginháwa nákung
pangítà) ug sápì apan kamu nagsígi
lang ug ínum,</i> I wear myself out earning
money, and all you do is drink. <b>1f</b> <b>-- ra pud
núun</b> that's the only thing that's wrong
with it. <i>'Dì man pasulayan sa dì pa mapalit.'--'Mau
ra pud núun,'</i> 'It's good, but you
can't try it out before you buy it.'--'That's
the only thing that is wrong with it.' <b>1g</b> <b>-y
(ang) pag-[<i>verb</i>]</b>, <b>i-[<i>verb</i>]</b> is the time [so-and-so]
happens. <i>Mauy ipanangpit níya
manday human na,</i> He calls you after he's
finished eating. <i>Pag-adtu níya mau say pag-adtu
nákù,</i> When he went was the time I
went, too. <b>1g1</b> <b>-- pa</b> <i>see</i> <sc>PA-</sc>, <i>2e</i>, <i>8b</i>. <b>1h</b> <b>--
nga [<i>noun</i>]</b> the aforementioned, said. <i>Wà
ku makaila sa maung táwu,</i> I don't know
that particular person. <b>1i</b> <b>-- pay ... -- pay</b>
even though [such-and-such] is the case, [so-and-so]
is true of the same person anyway.
<i>Mu pay mangáyù mu pay mangísug,</i> He asks
a favor, and yet he has the nerve to get angry.
<b>2</b> <b>-- nga [<i>sentence</i>]</b> therefore, consequently.
<i>Sígi kung praktis, mau nà nga maáyu
kung mubayli,</i> I always practice. That's
why I dance well. <i>Sa ámù kanúnay nga mangísug
si Máma. Mau gánì nga dílì layhang
mupaúlì si Pápa,</i> Mother is always angry at
home. That is why even Dad doesn't like to
go home. <b>3</b> <b>-- ra</b> no more, that's all. <i>'Adúna
pay láin?'--'Mau ra,'</i> 'Is there any more?'--'That's
all there is.' <b>3a</b> <b>-- ra nga</b> the
same. <i>Mau rang klasíha nà. Purus tagdiyis,</i>
Those are of the same class. They are all
ten cents apiece. <b>4</b> <b>-- ra ug</b> <b>4a</b> it seems. <i>Mu
rag láin nà,</i> It seems to be a different one.
-----File: 1392.png--------------------------------------------------------
<b>4b</b> rather. <i>Mu rag giuhaw ku,</i> I am rather
thirsty. <i>Ang báhù dílì mangga, mau rag
nangkà hinúun,</i> The smell is not that of the
mango, it is rather like that of the jackfruit.
<i>Mau ra ug nahuwasan na ku sa ákung kakulbà,</i>
I feel a bit relieved from my fright.
<b>4c</b> as if [so-and-so] were the case. <i>Nagpaduludiskursu
siya mu rag si kinsa,</i> He took
it upon himself to give a speech as though
he were s.o. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B1256] turn out to be
correct. <i>Gisulaysuláyan kug duut ang usa
sa mga timbri, namau bayà,</i> I tried pressing
one of the buttons at random. It happened
to be the right one. <b>2</b> [A13] be the same.
<i>Bísan ug atbang ta sa pulitika magmau lang
gihápun ang átung pagbinatiay,</i> Though we
are opponents in politics, our feelings towards
each other are still the same. <b>ka-</b> <i>v</i> [B1256; b8]
know how to do s.t. <i>Makamau
kang musulat?</i> Do you know how to write?
<i>Wà kuy nakamauhan,</i> I don't know anything.
<b>di-(<-)</b> <i>see</i> <sc>DIMÁU</sc>. <b>paka-</b> <i>v</i> [A13; a12]
pretend, consider s.t. as right or the one.
<i>Ngánung pakamauhun man nímu nga ang
ákù man ni?</i> Why do you insist this is the
very one, when it is mine? <b>maumáu</b> v [A; a12]
<b>1</b> make temporary repairs by just trying
things out, make do with s.t. less than
what is really needed. <i>Ug maáyu kang mumaumáu
ug áyu, mudágan giyud nang mutúra,</i>
If you are good at fiddling around
with your motorcycle, at least it will run. <b>2</b>
fabricate, make s.t. not real. <i>Sa mga kumunista
ang Diyus usa ka maumáu,</i> To the
communists, God is a figment of man's imagination.
<b>maumáu na sa ginháwa</b> = <sc>MAU</sc>,
<i>1e</i>.

<b>ma-un(<-)</b> affix added to verbs and adjectives
to form adjectives which mean 'having the
characteristic of doing or becoming [so-and-so]'.
<i>Malipáyun</i>, @Happy. <i>Maluyáhung tíngug,</i>
In a weak voice. <i>Mapangilyupúung
naghangyù sa Prisidinti nga luwasun ang
íyang anak,</i> With pleas she implored the
President to spare her son. <i>Mapasalígung
balità,</i> Reassuring news. <i>Matuhùtuhúun,</i>
@Gullible, @superstitious.

<b>máut</b> (from <i>daut</i>) <i>a</i> <b>1</b> @{not good}, @substandard

<b>may</b> <b>1</b> there is, are, was[** ,] were. <i>May tulu ka
táwung nangítà nímu,</i> There were three persons
looking for you. <i>Kun may isúgù,</i> At

<b>2</b> @have. <i>May sigarilyu ka dihà?</i> Do you have
any cigarettes on you? <b>2a</b> <b>may pagka-</b> be
somewhat. <i>May pagkatabian ni si Áning,</i>
Aning is somewhat talkative. <b>2b</b> <b>-- idad</b> be

He is already of age and he can vote now. <b>3</b>
near a place. <i>Didtu siya magtindug sa may
pultahan,</i> He was standing there by the
door. <b>4</b> some, [so-and-so] long ago, <i>May
duha ka búwan na níyang trabáhu dinhi,</i>
He's been working here for about two
months now. <b>4a</b> <b>-- mga</b> at about [such-and-such]
a time. <i>Didtu siya sa may mga alas
kwatru,</i> He was there at around four. <b>-- láin
pa</b> yes, of course (is there anything or anyone
else). <i>Siya giyuy nagkúhà sa libru kay
siya ra may dihà. May láin pa?</i> He must have
taken the book because he was the only
one there. Who else could have? <i>Kan-un giyud
ni níya. May láin pa?</i> He'll eat this,
don't worry. Would he fail to do so!

<b>midiya</b> @half. <i>Midiya pulgáda ang gibag-un,</i>
Half an inch thick. <i>Midiya ang bátà sa sinihan,</i>
A child pays half fare in the movies.
<i>Midiya kílu nga karni,</i> Half a kilo of meat.
i- thirty minutes after the hour. <i>Alas dus imidiya,</i>
Two thirty. <i>v</i> [B56] get to be to
-----File: 1397.png--------------------------------------------------------
the half hour. <i>'Alas singku na ba?'--'Mumidiya
